      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Island country in the Caribbean
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       This article is about the country in the Caribbean. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Barbados_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Barbados (disambiguation)">Barbados (disambiguation)</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Barbuda" title="Barbuda">Barbuda</a> or <a href="/wiki/Barbatos" title="Barbatos">Barbatos</a>.
      </div>

      <p><b>Barbados</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɑːr/: 'ar' in 'far'">ɑːr</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Barbados.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4b/En-us-Barbados.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Barbados.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span> or <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>/</a></span></span>) is an <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a> of the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> region of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>. It is 34 kilometres (21 miles) in length and up to 23&nbsp;km (14&nbsp;mi) in width, covering an area of 432&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (167&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). It is in the western area of the North Atlantic and 100&nbsp;km (62&nbsp;mi) east of the <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> therein, Barbados is the most easterly of the Caribbean Islands. Barbados is east of the Windwards, part of the Lesser Antilles, roughly at <a href="/wiki/13th_parallel_north" title="13th parallel north">13°N</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a>. It is about 168&nbsp;km (104&nbsp;mi) east of both the countries of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a> and 180&nbsp;km (110&nbsp;mi) south-east of <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> and 400&nbsp;km (250&nbsp;mi) north-east of <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>. Barbados is outside the principal Atlantic <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_belt" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane belt">hurricane belt</a>. Its capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Bridgetown,_Barbados" class="mw-redirect" title="Bridgetown, Barbados">Bridgetown</a>. </p>
      <p>Inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Caribs">Kalinago</a> people since the 13th century, and prior to that by other <a href="/wiki/Amerindian" class="mw-redirect" title="Amerindian">Amerindians</a>, Barbados was visited by Spanish navigators in the late 15th century and claimed for the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Spain" title="Monarchy of Spain">Spanish Crown</a>. It first appeared on a Spanish map in 1511.<sup id="cite_ref-Spanish_Main_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spanish_Main-8">[8]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> claimed the island between 1532 and 1536, but later abandoned it in 1620 with their only remnants being an introduction of wild boars for a good supply of meat whenever the island was visited. An <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">English</a> ship, the <i>Olive Blossom</i>, arrived in Barbados on 14 May 1625; its men took possession of it in the name of <a href="/wiki/James_VI_and_I" title="James VI and I">King James I</a>. In 1627, the first permanent settlers arrived from England, and it became an <a href="/wiki/English_overseas_possessions" title="English overseas possessions">English</a> and later <a href="/wiki/British_colonisation_of_the_Americas#British_Caribbean_colonies" class="mw-redirect" title="British colonisation of the Americas">British colony</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Commonwealth_History_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Commonwealth_History-9">[9]</a></sup> As a wealthy sugar colony, it became an English centre of the <a href="/wiki/African_slave_trade" class="mw-redirect" title="African slave trade">African slave trade</a> until that trade was outlawed by the <a href="/wiki/Slave_Trade_Act_1807" title="Slave Trade Act 1807">Slave Trade Act 1807</a>, with final emancipation of slaves in Barbados occurring over a period of years following the <a href="/wiki/Slavery_Abolition_Act_1833" title="Slavery Abolition Act 1833">Slavery Abolition Act 1833</a>. </p>
      <p>On 30 November 1966, Barbados became an independent state and <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realm</a> with <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> as <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Barbados" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen of Barbados">its queen</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> though the country is set to remove her as its head of state and become a republic by 30 November 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> It has a population of 287,010 people, predominantly of African descent. Despite being classified as an Atlantic island, Barbados is considered to be a part of the Caribbean, where it is ranked as a leading tourist destination. Of the tourists, 40% come from the UK, with the US and Canada making up the next large groups of visitors to the island.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The name "Barbados" is from either the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> term <i lang="pt" title="Portuguese-language text">os barbudos</i> or the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> equivalent, <i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">los barbudos</i>, both meaning "the bearded ones". It is unclear whether "bearded" refers to the long, hanging roots of the bearded <a href="/wiki/Fig-tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Fig-tree">fig-tree</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Ficus_citrifolia" title="Ficus citrifolia">Ficus citrifolia</a></i>), indigenous to the island, or to the allegedly bearded <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Caribs">Caribs</a> who once inhabited the island, or, more fancifully, to a visual impression of a beard formed by the sea foam that sprays over the outlying reefs. In 1519, a map produced by the <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoese</a> mapmaker <a href="/wiki/Visconte_Maggiolo" title="Visconte Maggiolo">Visconte Maggiolo</a> showed and named Barbados in its correct position. Furthermore, the island of <a href="/wiki/Barbuda" title="Barbuda">Barbuda</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leewards</a> is very similar in name and was once named "<span lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">Las Barbudas</span>" by the Spanish. </p>
      <p>The original name for Barbados in the <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era" title="Pre-Columbian era">Pre-Columbian era</a> was <i lang="awd" title="Arawakan languages collective text">Ichirouganaim</i>, according to accounts by descendants of the indigenous <a href="/wiki/Arawakan_languages" title="Arawakan languages">Arawakan</a>-speaking tribes in other regional areas, with possible translations including "Red land with white teeth"<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> or "Redstone island with teeth outside (reefs)"<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> or simply "Teeth".<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Colloquially, Barbadians refer to their home island as "Bim" or other nicknames associated with Barbados, including "Bimshire". The origin is uncertain, but several theories exist. The <a href="/wiki/National_Cultural_Foundation" title="National Cultural Foundation">National Cultural Foundation</a> of Barbados says that "Bim" was a word commonly used by <a href="/wiki/Slave" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave">slaves</a>, and that it derives from the <a href="/wiki/Igbo_language" title="Igbo language">Igbo</a> term <i lang="ig" title="Igbo-language text">bém</i> from <i lang="ig" title="Igbo-language text">bé mụ́</i> meaning 'my home, kindred, kind',<sup id="cite_ref-Carrington,_Sean_2007_25_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrington,_Sean_2007_25-18">[18]</a></sup> the Igbo phoneme <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[e]</a></span> in the Igbo orthography is very close to <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span></span>/</a></span></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Allsopp2003_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Allsopp2003-19">[19]</a></sup> The name could have arisen due to the relatively large percentage of enslaved <a href="/wiki/Igbo_people" title="Igbo people">Igbo people</a> from modern-day southeastern <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> arriving in Barbados in the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-EltisRichardson1997_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EltisRichardson1997-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The words 'Bim' and 'Bimshire' are recorded in the <i><a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">Oxford English Dictionary</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Chambers_Dictionary" title="Chambers Dictionary">Chambers Twentieth Century Dictionaries</a></i>. Another possible source for 'Bim' is reported to be in the <i>Agricultural Reporter</i> of 25 April 1868, where the Rev. N. Greenidge (father of one of the island's most famous scholars, <a href="/wiki/Abel_Hendy_Jones_Greenidge" class="mw-redirect" title="Abel Hendy Jones Greenidge">Abel Hendy Jones Greenidge</a>) suggested the listing of Bimshire as a county of England. Expressly named were "Wiltshire, Hampshire, Berkshire and Bimshire".<sup id="cite_ref-Carrington,_Sean_2007_25_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrington,_Sean_2007_25-18">[18]</a></sup> Lastly, in the <i>Daily Argosy</i> (of Demerara, i.e. Guyana) of 1652, there is a reference to Bim as a possible corruption of 'Byam', the name of a Royalist leader against the Parliamentarians. That source suggested the followers of Byam became known as 'Bims' and that this became a word for all Barbadians.<sup id="cite_ref-Carrington,_Sean_2007_25_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrington,_Sean_2007_25-18">[18]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Barbados" title="History of Barbados">History of Barbados</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-colonial_period">Pre-colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pre-colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Archeological evidence suggests humans may have first settled or visited the island circa 1600 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> More permanent <a href="/wiki/Amerindian" class="mw-redirect" title="Amerindian">Amerindian</a> settlement of Barbados dates to about the 4th to 7th centuries AD, by a group known as the <a href="/wiki/Saladoid" title="Saladoid">Saladoid</a>-Barrancoid.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The two main groups were the <a href="/wiki/Arawaks" class="mw-redirect" title="Arawaks">Arawaks</a> from South America, who became dominant around 800–1200 AD, and the more war-like <a href="/wiki/Kalinago" title="Kalinago">Kalinago</a> (<a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Caribs">Island Caribs</a>) who arrived from South America in the 12th–13th centuries<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_arrival">European arrival</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: European arrival">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:1632_Cardona_Descripcion_Indias_(11).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/1632_Cardona_Descripcion_Indias_%2811%29.jpg/220px-1632_Cardona_Descripcion_Indias_%2811%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/1632_Cardona_Descripcion_Indias_%2811%29.jpg/330px-1632_Cardona_Descripcion_Indias_%2811%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/1632_Cardona_Descripcion_Indias_%2811%29.jpg/440px-1632_Cardona_Descripcion_Indias_%2811%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3184" data-file-height="2165"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:1632_Cardona_Descripcion_Indias_(11).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> claimed Barbados from 1532 until 1620.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>It is uncertain which European nation arrived first in Barbados, which probably would have been at some point in the 15th century or 16th century. One lesser-known source points to earlier revealed works predating contemporary sources indicating it could have been the Spanish.<sup id="cite_ref-Spanish_Main_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spanish_Main-8">[8]</a></sup> Many, if not most, believe the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal_(1415-1542)" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Portugal (1415-1542)">Portuguese</a>, en route to <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> were the first Europeans to come upon the island. The island was largely ignored by Europeans, though Spanish slave raiding is thought to have reduced the native population, with many fleeing to other islands.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="English_settlement_in_the_1600s">English settlement in the 1600s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: English settlement in the 1600s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:GEORGE_WASHINGTON_HOUSE_-_BARBADOS.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/GEORGE_WASHINGTON_HOUSE_-_BARBADOS.jpg/220px-GEORGE_WASHINGTON_HOUSE_-_BARBADOS.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/GEORGE_WASHINGTON_HOUSE_-_BARBADOS.jpg/330px-GEORGE_WASHINGTON_HOUSE_-_BARBADOS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/GEORGE_WASHINGTON_HOUSE_-_BARBADOS.jpg/440px-GEORGE_WASHINGTON_HOUSE_-_BARBADOS.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1964"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:GEORGE_WASHINGTON_HOUSE_-_BARBADOS.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/George_Washington_House_(Barbados)" title="George Washington House (Barbados)">George Washington House</a> was visited by <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a> in 1751, in what is believed to have been his only trip outside the present-day <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-boston_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boston-28">[28]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The first English ship, which had arrived on 14 May 1625, was captained by John Powell. The first settlement began on 17 February 1627, near what is now <a href="/wiki/Holetown" title="Holetown">Holetown</a> (formerly Jamestown),<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> by a group led by John Powell's younger brother, Henry, consisting of 80 settlers and 10 English indentured laborers.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Some sources state that some Africans were amongst these first settlers.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The settlement was established as a <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_colony" title="Proprietary colony">proprietary colony</a> and funded by Sir <a href="/wiki/William_Courten" title="William Courten">William Courten</a>, a <a href="/wiki/City_of_London" title="City of London">City of London</a> merchant who acquired the title to Barbados and several other islands. So the first colonists were actually tenants and much of the profits of their labour returned to Courten and his company.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Courten's title was later transferred to <a href="/wiki/James_Hay,_1st_Earl_of_Carlisle" title="James Hay, 1st Earl of Carlisle">James Hay, 1st Earl of Carlisle</a>, in what was called the "Great Barbados Robbery."<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Carlisle then chose as governor <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hawley_(governor)" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry Hawley (governor)">Henry Hawley</a>, who established the <a href="/wiki/Barbados_House_of_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbados House of Assembly">House of Assembly</a> in 1639, in an effort to appease the planters, who might otherwise have opposed his controversial appointment.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Slavery_and_Economy_in_Barbados_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Slavery_and_Economy_in_Barbados-33">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the period 1640–60, the West Indies attracted over two-thirds of the total number of English emigrants to the Americas. By 1650 there were 44,000 settlers in the West Indies, as compared to 12,000 on the <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">Chesapeake</a> and 23,000 in <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a>. Most English arrivals were indentured. After five years of labour, they were given "freedom dues" of about £10, usually in goods. Before the mid-1630s, they also received 5 to 10 acres (2 to 4 hectares) of land, but after that time the island filled and there was no more free land. During the <a href="/wiki/Interregnum_(England)" title="Interregnum (England)">Cromwellian era</a> (1650s) this included a large number of prisoners-of-war, vagrants and people who were illicitly kidnapped, who were forcibly transported to the island and sold as servants. These last two groups were predominantly Irish, as several thousand were infamously rounded up by English merchants and sold into servitude in Barbados and other Caribbean islands during this period, a practice that came to be known as being <i>Barbadosed</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Slavery_and_Economy_in_Barbados_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Slavery_and_Economy_in_Barbados-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Cultivation of tobacco, cotton, <a href="/wiki/Ginger" title="Ginger">ginger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indigo" title="Indigo">indigo</a> was thus handled primarily by European indentured labour until the start of the <a href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a> industry in the 1640s and the growing reliance on and importation of enslaved Africans. </p>
      <p>Life in the young colony was not easy, with parish registers from the 1650s show, for the white population, there were four times as many deaths as marriages. The mainstay of the infant colony's economy was the growth export of tobacco, but tobacco prices eventually fell in the 1630s as Chesapeake production expanded.<sup id="cite_ref-Slavery_and_Economy_in_Barbados_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Slavery_and_Economy_in_Barbados-33">[33]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_of_the_English_Civil_War">Effects of the English Civil War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Effects of the English Civil War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/English_Revolution_in_the_Colonies" class="mw-redirect" title="English Revolution in the Colonies">English Revolution in the Colonies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Restoration_(Colonies)" class="mw-redirect" title="Restoration (Colonies)">Restoration (Colonies)</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Around the same time, fighting during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Three_Kingdoms" class="mw-redirect" title="War of the Three Kingdoms">War of the Three Kingdoms</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Interregnum_(England)" title="Interregnum (England)">Interregnum</a> spilled over into Barbados and Barbadian territorial waters. The island was not <a href="/wiki/English_Revolution_in_the_Colonies" class="mw-redirect" title="English Revolution in the Colonies">involved in the war</a> until after the execution of <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">Charles I</a>, when the island's government fell under the control of Royalists (ironically the Governor, Philip Bell, remaining loyal to <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_England" title="Parliament of England">Parliament</a> while the Barbadian <a href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly" title="House of Assembly">House of Assembly</a>, under the influence of Humphrey Walrond, supported <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles II</a>). To try to bring the recalcitrant colony to heel, the <a href="/wiki/Rump_Parliament#Commonwealth_of_England" title="Rump Parliament">Commonwealth Parliament</a> passed an act on 3 October 1650 prohibiting trade between England and Barbados, and because the island also traded with the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, further <a href="/wiki/Navigation_acts" class="mw-redirect" title="Navigation acts">navigation acts</a> were passed prohibiting any but English vessels trading with <a href="/wiki/Dutch_colonies#Atlantic" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch colonies">Dutch colonies</a>. These acts were a precursor to the <a href="/wiki/First_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="First Anglo-Dutch War">First Anglo-Dutch War</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_England" title="Commonwealth of England">Commonwealth of England</a> sent an invasion force under the command of <a href="/wiki/George_Ayscue" title="George Ayscue">Sir George Ayscue</a>, which arrived in October 1651. Ayscue with a smaller force which included Scottish prisoners surprised a larger force of Royalists, but had to resort to spying and diplomacy ultimately. On January 11, 1652, the Royalists in the House of Assembly led by <a href="/wiki/Francis_Willoughby,_5th_Baron_Willoughby_of_Parham" title="Francis Willoughby, 5th Baron Willoughby of Parham">Lord Willoughby</a> surrendered which marked the end of royalist privateering as a major threat.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> The conditions of the surrender were incorporated into the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Charter_of_Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Charter of Barbados (page does not exist)">Charter of Barbados</a> (Treaty of Oistins), which was signed at the Mermaid's Inn, <a href="/wiki/Oistins" title="Oistins">Oistins</a>, on 17 January 1652.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Lord Nelson Statue was removed from Bridgetown on November 16th, 2020. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Irish_people_in_Barbados">Irish people in Barbados</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Irish people in Barbados">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Irish_people_in_Barbados" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish people in Barbados">Irish people in Barbados</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Starting with Cromwell, a large percentage of the white labourer population were indentured servants and involuntarily transported people from Ireland. Irish servants in Barbados were often treated poorly, and Barbadian planters gained a reputation for cruelty.<sup id="cite_ref-Monahan_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Monahan-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>55</span></sup> The decreased appeal of an indenture on Barbados, combined with enormous demand for labour caused by sugar cultivation, led the use of involuntary transportation to Barbados as a punishment for crimes, or for political prisoners, and also to the kidnapping of labourers who were sent to Barbados involuntarily.<sup id="cite_ref-Monahan_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Monahan-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>55</span></sup> Irish indentured servants were a significant portion of the population throughout the period when white servants were used for plantation labour in Barbados, and while a "steady stream" of Irish servants entered the Barbados throughout the seventeenth century, Cromwellian efforts to pacify Ireland created a "veritable tidal wave" of Irish labourers who were sent to Barbados during the 1650s.<sup id="cite_ref-Monahan_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Monahan-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>56</span></sup> Due to inadequate historical records, the total number of Irish labourers sent to Barbados is unknown, and estimates have been "highly contentious."<sup id="cite_ref-Monahan_37-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Monahan-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>56</span></sup> While one historical source estimated that as many as 50,000 Irish people were transported to either Barbados or Virginia unwillingly during the 1650s, this estimate is "quite likely exaggerated."<sup id="cite_ref-Monahan_37-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Monahan-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>56</span></sup> Another estimate that 12,000 Irish prisoners had arrived in Barbados by 1655 has been described as "probably exaggerated" by historian Richard B. Sheridan.<sup id="cite_ref-Sheridan_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sheridan-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>236</span></sup> According to historian Thomas Bartlett, it is "generally accepted" that approximately 10,000 Irish were sent to the West Indies involuntarily, and approximately 40,000 came as voluntary indentured servants, while many also travelled as voluntary, un-indentured emigrants.<sup id="cite_ref-Bartlett_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bartlett-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>256</span></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_sugar_revolution">The sugar revolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: The sugar revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The introduction of <a href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a> from <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Brazil" title="Dutch Brazil">Dutch Brazil</a> in 1640 completely transformed society, the economy and the physical landscape. Barbados eventually had one of the world's biggest sugar industries.<sup id="cite_ref-beyond_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beyond-40">[40]</a></sup> One group instrumental in ensuring the early success of the industry was the <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">Sephardic Jews</a>, who had originally been expelled from the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Iberian peninsula">Iberian peninsula</a>, to end up in <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Brazil" title="Dutch Brazil">Dutch Brazil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-beyond_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beyond-40">[40]</a></sup> As the effects of the new crop increased, so did the shift in the ethnic composition of Barbados and surrounding islands.<sup id="cite_ref-Slavery_and_Economy_in_Barbados_33-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Slavery_and_Economy_in_Barbados-33">[33]</a></sup> The workable sugar plantation required a large investment and a great deal of heavy labour. At first, Dutch traders supplied the equipment, financing, and enslaved Africans, in addition to transporting most of the sugar to Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-Slavery_and_Economy_in_Barbados_33-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Slavery_and_Economy_in_Barbados-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> In 1644 the population of Barbados was estimated at 30,000, of which about 800 were of African descent, with the remainder mainly of English descent. These English smallholders were eventually bought out and the island filled up with large sugar plantations worked by enslaved Africans.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> By 1660 there was near parity with 27,000 blacks and 26,000 whites. By 1666 at least 12,000 white smallholders had been bought out, died, or left the island, many choosing to emigrate to <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> or the <a href="/wiki/American_Colonies" class="mw-redirect" title="American Colonies">American Colonies</a> (notably the Carolinas).<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> As a result, Barbados enacted a <a href="/wiki/Barbados_Slave_Code" title="Barbados Slave Code">slave code</a> as a way of legislatively controlling its black enslaved population.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> The law's text was influential in laws in other colonies.<sup id="cite_ref-menard_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-menard-42">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>By 1680 there were 20,000 free whites and 46,000 enslaved Africans;<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> by 1724, there were 18,000 free whites and 55,000 enslaved Africans.<sup id="cite_ref-Slavery_and_Economy_in_Barbados_33-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Slavery_and_Economy_in_Barbados-33">[33]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="18th_and_19th_centuries">18th and 19th centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 18th and 19th centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bussa_statue.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Bussa_statue.png/170px-Bussa_statue.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Bussa_statue.png/255px-Bussa_statue.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Bussa_statue.png/340px-Bussa_statue.png 2x" data-file-width="476" data-file-height="637"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bussa_statue.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Bussa_Emancipation_Statue" title="Bussa Emancipation Statue">Statue of Bussa</a>, Bridgetown. Bussa led the largest slave rebellion in Barbadian history.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The harsh conditions endured by the slaves resulted in several planned slave rebellions, the largest of which was <a href="/wiki/Bussa%27s_rebellion" title="Bussa's rebellion">Bussa's rebellion</a> in 1816 which was suppressed by British troops.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> Growing opposition to slavery led to its abolition in the British Empire in 1833.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> However the plantocracy class retained control of the political and economic situation on the island, with most workers living in relative poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Great_Hurricane_of_1780" title="Great Hurricane of 1780">1780 hurricane</a> killed over 4,000 people on Barbados.<sup id="cite_ref-pr_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pr-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-deadliest_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deadliest-44">[44]</a></sup> In 1854, a <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a> epidemic killed over 20,000 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="20th_century_.E2.80.93_colonial_period"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century_–_colonial_period">20th century – colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 20th century – colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Deep dissatisfaction with the situation on Barbados led many to emigrate.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Things came to a head in the 1930s during the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, as Barbadians began demanding better conditions for workers, the legalisation of trade unions and a widening of the franchise, which at that point was limited to male property owners.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> As a result of the increasing unrest the British sent a commission (The West Indies Royal Commission, or Moyne Commission) in 1938, which recommended enacting many of the requested reforms on the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> As a result, Afro-Barbadians began to play a much more prominent role in the colony's politics, with universal suffrage being introduced in 1950.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Prominent among these early activists was <a href="/wiki/Grantley_Herbert_Adams" title="Grantley Herbert Adams">Grantley Herbert Adams</a>, who helped found the <a href="/wiki/Barbados_Labour_Party" title="Barbados Labour Party">Barbados Labour Party</a> (BLP) in 1938.<sup id="cite_ref-dnation_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dnation-47">[47]</a></sup> He became the first Premier of Barbados in 1953, followed by fellow BLP-founder <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Gordon_Cummins" title="Hugh Gordon Cummins">Hugh Gordon Cummins</a> from 1958 to 1961. A group of left-leaning politicians who advocated swifter moves to independence broke off from the BLP and founded the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Labour_Party_(Barbados)" title="Democratic Labour Party (Barbados)">Democratic Labour Party</a> (DLP) in 1955.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DN_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DN-49">[49]</a></sup> The DLP subsequently won the <a href="/wiki/1961_Barbadian_general_election" title="1961 Barbadian general election">1961 Barbadian general election</a> and their leader <a href="/wiki/Errol_Barrow" title="Errol Barrow">Errol Barrow</a> became premier. </p>
      <p>Full internal self-government was enacted in 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> Barbados joined the short-lived <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a> from 1958 to 1962, later gaining full independence on 30 November 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> Errol Barrow became the country's first prime minister. Barbados opted to remain within the <a href="/wiki/British_Commonwealth" class="mw-redirect" title="British Commonwealth">British Commonwealth</a>, retaining Queen Elizabeth as <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Barbados" title="Monarchy of Barbados">Monarch</a>, represented locally by a <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Barbados" title="Governor-General of Barbados">governor-general</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-independence_era">Post-independence era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Post-independence era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Barrow government sought to diversify the economy away from agriculture, seeking to boost industry and the tourism sector. Barbados was also at forefront of regional integration efforts, spearheading the creation of <a href="/wiki/CARIFTA" class="mw-redirect" title="CARIFTA">CARIFTA</a> and <a href="/wiki/CARICOM" class="mw-redirect" title="CARICOM">CARICOM</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> The DLP lost the <a href="/wiki/1976_Barbadian_general_election" title="1976 Barbadian general election">1976 Barbadian general election</a> to the BLP under <a href="/wiki/Tom_Adams_(politician)" title="Tom Adams (politician)">Tom Adams</a>. Adams adopted a more conservative and strongly pro-Western stance, allowing the Americans to use Barbados as the launchpad for their <a href="/wiki/United_States_invasion_of_Grenada" title="United States invasion of Grenada">invasion of Grenada</a> in 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Adams died in office in 1985 and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Harold_Bernard_St._John" title="Harold Bernard St. John">Harold Bernard St. John</a>, however he lost the <a href="/wiki/1986_Barbadian_general_election" title="1986 Barbadian general election">1986 Barbadian general election</a> which saw the return of the DLP under Errol Barrow, who had been highly critical of the US intervention in Grenada. However Barrow too died in office, and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Erskine_Sandiford" title="Lloyd Erskine Sandiford">Lloyd Erskine Sandiford</a> who remained Prime Minister until 1994. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Owen_Arthur" title="Owen Arthur">Owen Arthur</a> of the BLP won the <a href="/wiki/1994_Barbadian_general_election" title="1994 Barbadian general election">1994 Barbadian general election</a>, remaining Prime Minister until 2008. Arthur was a strong advocate of republicanism, though a planned referendum to replace Queen Elizabeth as Head of State in 2008 never took place.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn_republic_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn_republic-51">[51]</a></sup> The DLP won the <a href="/wiki/2008_Barbadian_general_election" title="2008 Barbadian general election">2008 Barbadian general election</a>, however the new Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/David_Thompson_(Barbadian_politician)" title="David Thompson (Barbadian politician)">David Thompson</a> died in 2010 and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Freundel_Stuart" title="Freundel Stuart">Freundel Stuart</a>. The BLP returned to power <a href="/wiki/2018_Barbadian_general_election" title="2018 Barbadian general election">in 2018</a> under <a href="/wiki/Mia_Mottley" title="Mia Mottley">Mia Mottley</a>, who became Barbados's first female Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Barbados announced on 15 September 2020 that it intends to become a republic by 30 November 2021, the 55th anniversary of its independence. It plans to replace the Queen with its own elected official as head of state. At this point, Barbados will cease to be a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realm</a>, but will maintain membership in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Critics claim that the move came about in part because China exerted pressure on Barbados.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geography and climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Barbados" title="Geography of Barbados">Geography of Barbados</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Barbados-2020_englisch.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Barbados-2020_englisch.png/220px-Barbados-2020_englisch.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="281" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Barbados-2020_englisch.png/330px-Barbados-2020_englisch.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Barbados-2020_englisch.png/440px-Barbados-2020_englisch.png 2x" data-file-width="943" data-file-height="1205"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Barbados-2020_englisch.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of Barbados
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Barbados is situated in the Atlantic Ocean, east of the other <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a> Islands. Barbados is the easternmost island in the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>. It is flat in comparison to its island neighbours to the west, the <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a>. The island rises gently to the central highland region known as Scotland District, with the high point of the nation being <a href="/wiki/Mount_Hillaby" title="Mount Hillaby">Mount Hillaby</a> 340&nbsp;m (1,120&nbsp;ft) above sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the parish of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Michael,_Barbados" title="Saint Michael, Barbados">Saint Michael</a> lies Barbados's capital and main city, <a href="/wiki/Bridgetown" title="Bridgetown">Bridgetown</a>, containing 1/3 of the country's population.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> Other major towns scattered across the island include <a href="/wiki/Holetown" title="Holetown">Holetown</a>, in the parish of <a href="/wiki/Saint_James,_Barbados" title="Saint James, Barbados">Saint James</a>; <a href="/wiki/Oistins" title="Oistins">Oistins</a>, in the parish of <a href="/wiki/Christ_Church,_Barbados" title="Christ Church, Barbados">Christ Church</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Speightstown" title="Speightstown">Speightstown</a>, in the parish of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter,_Barbados" title="Saint Peter, Barbados">Saint Peter</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Barbados lies on the boundary of the <a href="/wiki/South_American_plate" class="mw-redirect" title="South American plate">South American</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Plate" title="Caribbean Plate">Caribbean Plates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Subduction" title="Subduction">subduction</a> of the South American plate beneath the Caribbean plate scrapes sediment from the South American plate and deposits it above the subduction zone forming an <a href="/wiki/Accretionary_wedge" title="Accretionary wedge">accretionary prism</a>. The rate of this depositing of material allows Barbados to rise at a rate of about 25&nbsp;mm (1&nbsp;in) per 1,000 years.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> This subduction means <a href="/wiki/Geology" title="Geology">geologically</a> the island is composed of <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">coral</a> roughly 90&nbsp;m (300&nbsp;ft) thick, where reefs formed above the sediment. The land slopes in a series of "terraces" in the west and goes into an incline in the east. A large proportion of the island is circled by <a href="/wiki/Coral_reefs" class="mw-redirect" title="Coral reefs">coral reefs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The erosion of limestone in the northeast of the island, in the Scotland District, has resulted in the formation of various caves and <a href="/wiki/Gully" title="Gully">gullies</a>. On the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic</a> east coast of the island <a href="/wiki/Coastal_landforms" class="mw-redirect" title="Coastal landforms">coastal landforms</a>, including stacks, have been created due to the limestone composition of the area. Also notable in the island is the rocky cape known as <a href="/wiki/Pico_Teneriffe_(Barbados)" title="Pico Teneriffe (Barbados)">Pico Teneriffe</a><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> or Pico de Tenerife, which is named after the fact that the island of <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a> in <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> is the first land east of Barbados according to the belief of the locals. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bathsheba,_Barbados_08.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Bathsheba%2C_Barbados_08.jpg/220px-Bathsheba%2C_Barbados_08.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Bathsheba%2C_Barbados_08.jpg/330px-Bathsheba%2C_Barbados_08.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Bathsheba%2C_Barbados_08.jpg/440px-Bathsheba%2C_Barbados_08.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bathsheba,_Barbados_08.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Bathsheba,_Saint_Joseph,_Barbados" class="mw-redirect" title="Bathsheba, Saint Joseph, Barbados">Bathsheba, Saint Joseph</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Crane_Beach.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Crane_Beach.JPG/220px-Crane_Beach.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Crane_Beach.JPG/330px-Crane_Beach.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Crane_Beach.JPG/440px-Crane_Beach.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2760" data-file-height="2048"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Crane_Beach.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Crane Beach is situated on the south east coast
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The country generally experiences two seasons, one of which includes noticeably higher rainfall. Known as the "<a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">wet season</a>", this period runs from June to December. By contrast, the "<a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry season</a>" runs from December to May. Annual precipitation ranges between 1,000 and 2,300&nbsp;mm (40 and 90&nbsp;in). From December to May the average temperatures range from 21 to 31&nbsp;°C (70 to 88&nbsp;°F), while between June and November, they range from 23 to 31&nbsp;°C (73 to 88&nbsp;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-weather1_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weather1-59">[59]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> scale, much of Barbados is regarded as a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_monsoon_climate" title="Tropical monsoon climate">tropical monsoon climate</a> (Am). However, breezes of 12 to 16&nbsp;km/h (7 to 10&nbsp;mph) abound throughout the year and give Barbados a <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> which is moderately tropical. </p>
      <p>Infrequent natural hazards include earthquakes, <a href="/wiki/Landslip" class="mw-redirect" title="Landslip">landslips</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hurricanes" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricanes">hurricanes</a>. Barbados is often spared the worst effects of the region's <a href="/wiki/Tropical_storm" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical storm">tropical storms</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricanes" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricanes">hurricanes</a> during the rainy season. Its location in the south-east of the Caribbean region puts the country just outside the principal <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_strike_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane strike zone">hurricane strike zone</a>. On average, a major hurricane strikes about once every 26 years. The last significant hit from a hurricane to cause severe damage to Barbados was <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Janet" title="Hurricane Janet">Hurricane Janet</a> in 1955; in 2010 the island was struck by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Tomas" title="Hurricane Tomas">Hurricane Tomas</a>, but this caused only minor damage across the country as it was only at Tropical Storm level of formation.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">Environmental issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Environmental issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:BarbadosFromISS.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/BarbadosFromISS.jpg/220px-BarbadosFromISS.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="332" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/BarbadosFromISS.jpg/330px-BarbadosFromISS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/BarbadosFromISS.jpg/440px-BarbadosFromISS.jpg 2x" data-file-width="679" data-file-height="1024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:BarbadosFromISS.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Barbados, seen from the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Barbados is susceptible to environmental pressures. As one of the world's most <a href="/wiki/List_of_island_countries_by_population_density" title="List of island countries by population density">densely populated isles</a>, the government worked during the 1990s<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> to aggressively integrate the growing south coast of the island into the Bridgetown Sewage Treatment Plant to reduce contamination of offshore coral reefs.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> As of the first decade of the 21st century, a second treatment plant has been proposed along the island's west coast. Being so densely populated, Barbados has made great efforts to protect its underground <a href="/wiki/Aquifer" title="Aquifer">aquifers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-barbadosadvocate.com_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-barbadosadvocate.com-64">[64]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As a coral-limestone island, Barbados is highly permeable to seepage of surface water into the earth. The government has placed great emphasis on protecting the catchment areas that lead directly into the huge network of underground aquifers and streams.<sup id="cite_ref-barbadosadvocate.com_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-barbadosadvocate.com-64">[64]</a></sup> On occasion illegal squatters have breached these areas, and the government has removed squatters to preserve the cleanliness of the underground springs which provide the island's drinking water.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The government has placed a huge emphasis on keeping Barbados clean with the aim of protecting the environment and preserving offshore coral reefs which surround the island. Many initiatives to mitigate human pressures on the coastal regions of Barbados and seas come from the Coastal Zone Management Unit (CZMU).<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Barbados has nearly 90 kilometres (56 miles) of coral reefs just offshore and two protected marine parks have been established off the west coast.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Overfishing is another threat which faces Barbados.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although on the opposite side of the Atlantic, and some 4,800 kilometres (3,000 miles) west of Africa, Barbados is one of many places in the American continent that experience heightened levels of <a href="/wiki/Mineral_dust" title="Mineral dust">mineral dust</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Sahara_Desert" class="mw-redirect" title="Sahara Desert">Sahara Desert</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Some particularly intense dust episodes have been blamed partly for the impacts on the health of coral reefs<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> surrounding Barbados or <a href="/wiki/Asthmatic" class="mw-redirect" title="Asthmatic">asthmatic</a> episodes,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> but evidence has not wholly supported the former such claim.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Access to <a href="/wiki/Biocapacity" title="Biocapacity">biocapacity</a> in Barbados is much lower than world average. In 2016, Barbados had 0.17 global hectares<sup id="cite_ref-footprintdata_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footprintdata-74">[74]</a></sup> of biocapacity per person within its territory, much less than the world average of 1.6 global hectares per person.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> In 2016 Barbados used 0.84 global hectares of biocapacity per person - their <a href="/wiki/Ecological_footprint" title="Ecological footprint">ecological footprint</a> of consumption. This means they use approximately five times as much biocapacity as Barbados contains. As a result, Barbados is running a biocapacity deficit.<sup id="cite_ref-footprintdata_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footprintdata-74">[74]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Barbados is host to four species of nesting turtles (<a href="/wiki/Green_turtles" class="mw-redirect" title="Green turtles">green turtles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loggerhead_sea_turtle" title="Loggerhead sea turtle">loggerheads</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hawksbill_turtle" class="mw-redirect" title="Hawksbill turtle">hawksbill turtles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Leatherbacks" class="mw-redirect" title="Leatherbacks">leatherbacks</a>) and has the second-largest hawksbill turtle-breeding population in the Caribbean.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> The driving of vehicles on beaches can crush nests buried in the sand and such activity is discouraged in nesting areas.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Barbados is also the host to the <a href="/wiki/Green_monkey" title="Green monkey">green monkey</a>. The green monkey is found in West Africa from Senegal to the Volta River. It has been introduced to the Cape Verde islands off north-western Africa, and the West Indian islands of Saint Kitts, Nevis, Saint Martin, and Barbados. It was introduced to the West Indies in the late 17th century when slave trade ships travelled to the Caribbean from West Africa. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Barbados" title="Demographics of Barbados">Demographics of Barbados</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbadians" title="Barbadians">Barbadians</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Barbados_bus_stop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Barbados_bus_stop.jpg/220px-Barbados_bus_stop.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Barbados_bus_stop.jpg/330px-Barbados_bus_stop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Barbados_bus_stop.jpg/440px-Barbados_bus_stop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="480"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Barbados_bus_stop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A bus stop in Barbados.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bridgetown_049.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Bridgetown_049.jpg/220px-Bridgetown_049.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Bridgetown_049.jpg/330px-Bridgetown_049.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Bridgetown_049.jpg/440px-Bridgetown_049.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bridgetown_049.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>People shopping in the capital Bridgetown.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The 2010 national census conducted by the Barbados Statistical Service reported a resident population of 277,821, of which 144,803 were female and 133,018 were male.<sup id="cite_ref-census_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-78">[78]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The life expectancy for Barbados residents as of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> is 79 years. The average life expectancy is 83 years for females and 78 years for males (2019).<sup id="cite_ref-cia_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-1">[1]</a></sup> Barbados and Japan have the highest per capita occurrences of <a href="/wiki/Centenarian" title="Centenarian">centenarians</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The crude birth rate is 12.23 births per 1,000 people, and the crude death rate is 8.39 deaths per 1,000 people. The infant mortality rate is 11.63 infant deaths per 1,000 live births. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Close to 90% of all Barbadians (also known colloquially as "Bajan") are of <a href="/wiki/Afro-Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Caribbean">Afro-Caribbean</a> descent ("<a href="/wiki/Afro-Barbadian" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Barbadian">Afro-Bajans</a>") and mixed descent. The remainder of the population includes groups of Europeans ("Anglo-Bajans" / "Euro-Bajans") mainly from the United Kingdom and Ireland, Italians, and Asians, predominantly Chinese and Indians (both Hindu and Muslim). Other groups in Barbados include people from the United Kingdom, United States and Canada. Barbadians who return after years of residence in the United States and children born in America to Bajan parents are called "Bajan Yankees", a term considered derogatory by some.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Generally, Bajans recognise and accept all "children of the island" as Bajans, and refer to each other as such. </p>
      <p>The biggest communities outside the Afro-Caribbean community are: </p> 
      <ol>
       <li>The <a href="/wiki/Indo-Guyanese" title="Indo-Guyanese">Indo-Guyanese</a>, an important part of the economy due to the increase of immigrants from partner country <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>. There are reports of a growing <a href="/wiki/Indians_in_Barbados" title="Indians in Barbados">Indo-Bajans</a> diaspora originating from Guyana and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> starting around 1990. Predominantly from southern India, they are growing in size but are smaller than the equivalent communities in Trinidad and Guyana. People who are Indians in the Caribbean are also referred to as <a href="/wiki/Coolie" title="Coolie">coolie</a> who are Indians that came from East India to the Americas as labourers. They sometimes get mixed up with <a href="/wiki/Dougla" class="mw-redirect" title="Dougla">dougla</a> who have African and Indian ancestry while coolies are full blooded Indians.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> The Muslim Barbadians of Indian origin are largely of <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarati</a> ancestry. Many small businesses in Barbados are run and operated by Muslim-Indian Bajans.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>Euro-Bajans (5% of the population)<sup id="cite_ref-cia_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-1">[1]</a></sup> have settled in Barbados since the 17th century, originating from England, Ireland, Portugal, and <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>. In 1643, there were 37,200 whites in Barbados (86% of the population).<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> More commonly they are known as "<a href="/wiki/White_Barbadian" title="White Barbadian">White Bajans</a>". Euro-Bajans introduced folk music, such as <a href="/wiki/Irish_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish music">Irish music</a> and Highland music, and certain place names, such as "Scotland District", a hilly region in the parish of St. Andrew. Among White Barbadians there exists an underclass known as <a href="/wiki/Redlegs" class="mw-redirect" title="Redlegs">Redlegs</a> comprising followers of the Duke of Monmouth after his defeat at the Battle of Sedgemoor, as well as the descendants of <a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">Irish</a> indentured labourers and prisoners imported to the island.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Many additionally moved on to become the earliest settlers of modern-day <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Carolina" title="Province of Carolina">North</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colonial_period_of_South_Carolina" title="Colonial period of South Carolina">South Carolina</a> in the United States. Today the Redlegs only number around 400.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>Chinese-Barbadians are a small portion of Barbados's wider Asian population.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> Most if not all first arrived in the 1940s from Hong Kong during the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Many Chinese-Bajans have the surnames Chin, Chynn or Lee, although other surnames prevail in certain areas of the island.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Chinese food and culture is becoming part of everyday Bajan culture.</li> 
       <li>Lebanese and Syrians form the island's <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arab</a> Barbadian community,<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> which is overwhelmingly Christian Arab. The Muslim Arab minority among Arab Barbadian make up a small percentage of the overall minority Muslim Barbadian population. The majority of the Lebanese and Syrians arrived in Barbados through trade opportunities. Their numbers are falling due to emigration to other countries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a> arrived in Barbados just after the first settlers in 1627. Bridgetown is the home of <a href="/wiki/Nidhe_Israel_Synagogue" title="Nidhe Israel Synagogue">Nidhe Israel Synagogue</a>, one of the oldest Jewish synagogues in the Americas, dating from 1654, though the current structure was erected in 1833, replacing one ruined by the hurricane of 1831.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Tombstones in the neighbouring cemetery date from the 1630s. Now under the care of the Barbados National Trust, the site was deserted in 1929 but was saved and restored by the Jewish community beginning in 1986.</li> 
       <li>In the seventeenth century, <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani people</a> were sent from the United Kingdom to work as slaves in the plantations in Barbados.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></li>
      </ol> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>English is the <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> of Barbados, and is used for communications, administration, and public services all over the island. In its capacity as the official language of the country, the standard of English tends to conform to the vocabulary, pronunciations, spellings, and conventions akin to, but not exactly the same as, those of <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">British English</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Barbados" title="Religion in Barbados">Religion in Barbados</a>
      </div>
