          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#89CFF0; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Church of God (1.99%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:teal; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Jehovah's witnesses (1.96%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:lightgreen; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Moravian (1.34%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:red; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Rastafarian (1.14%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:green; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Muslim (0.66%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:violet; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Brethren (0.64%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:crimson; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Salvation Army (0.42%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:orange; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Hindu (0.34%)
         </div> 
        </div> 
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Most Barbadians of African and European descent are Christians (95%), the largest denomination being <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Communion" title="Anglican Communion">Anglican</a> (40%).<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> Other Christian denominations with significant followings in Barbados are the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> (administered by <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Bridgetown" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Bridgetown">Roman Catholic Diocese of Bridgetown</a>), <a href="/wiki/Pentecostals" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostals">Pentecostals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witness" class="mw-redirect" title="Jehovah's Witness">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist Church</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spiritual_Baptist" title="Spiritual Baptist">Spiritual Baptists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> was the official state religion until its legal disestablishment by the Parliament of Barbados following independence.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Other religions in Barbados include <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Barbados" title="Islam in Barbados">Islam</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí Faith</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Barbados" title="History of the Jews in Barbados">Judaism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bridgetown_barbados_parliament_building.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Bridgetown_barbados_parliament_building.jpg/220px-Bridgetown_barbados_parliament_building.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Bridgetown_barbados_parliament_building.jpg/330px-Bridgetown_barbados_parliament_building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Bridgetown_barbados_parliament_building.jpg/440px-Bridgetown_barbados_parliament_building.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bridgetown_barbados_parliament_building.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Parliament_Buildings_(Barbados)" title="Parliament Buildings (Barbados)">Barbados parliament building</a> in Bridgetown
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Barbados" title="Government of Barbados">Government of Barbados</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Barbados" title="Politics of Barbados">Politics of Barbados</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Barbados has been an independent country since 30 November 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> It functions as a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary democracy">parliamentary democracy</a> modelled on the British <a href="/wiki/Westminster_system" title="Westminster system">Westminster system</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Barbados" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen of Barbados">Queen of Barbados</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a>, is <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and is represented locally by the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Barbados" title="Governor-General of Barbados">Governor-General of Barbados</a>—presently <a href="/wiki/Sandra_Mason" title="Sandra Mason">Sandra Mason</a>. Both are advised on matters of the Barbadian state by the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Barbados" title="Prime Minister of Barbados">Prime Minister of Barbados</a>, who is <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. There are 30 representatives within the <a href="/wiki/Barbados_House_of_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbados House of Assembly">House of Assembly</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Barbados" title="Constitution of Barbados">Constitution of Barbados</a> is the supreme law of the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The Attorney General heads <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Barbados" title="Judiciary of Barbados">the independent judiciary</a>. New Acts are passed by the Barbadian Parliament and require <a href="/wiki/Royal_assent" title="Royal assent">royal assent</a> by the governor-general to become law. </p>
      <p>During the 1990s at the suggestion of <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Manning" title="Patrick Manning">Patrick Manning</a>, Barbados attempted a <a href="/wiki/Political_union" title="Political union">political union</a> with Trinidad and Tobago and <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>. The project stalled after the then prime minister of Barbados, <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Erskine_Sandiford" title="Lloyd Erskine Sandiford">Lloyd Erskine Sandiford</a>, became ill and his <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Labour_Party_(Barbados)" title="Democratic Labour Party (Barbados)">Democratic Labour Party</a> lost the next general election.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Barbados continues to share close ties with Trinidad and Tobago and with Guyana, claiming the highest number of Guyanese immigrants after the United States, Canada and the United Kingdom. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Political culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Barbados functions as a <a href="/wiki/Two-party_system" title="Two-party system">two-party system</a>. The dominant political parties are the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Labour_Party_(Barbados)" title="Democratic Labour Party (Barbados)">Democratic Labour Party</a> and the incumbent <a href="/wiki/Barbados_Labour_Party" title="Barbados Labour Party">Barbados Labour Party</a>. Since Independence on 30 November 1966, the Democratic Labour Party (DLP) has governed from 1966 to 1976; 1986 to 1994; and from 2008 to 2018; and the Barbados Labour Party (BLP) has also governed from 1976 to 1986; 1994 to 2008; and from 2018 to present. The Democratic Labour Party government (DLP) held office with the then Premier of Barbados became Prime Minister of Barbados, Errol Barrow for three successive terms from 4 December 1961 to 2 September 1976; and again from 28 May 1986 until his sudden death in office on 1 June 1987. The 4th Prime Minister, Sir. Lloyd Sandiford took over with the Democratic Labour Party government (DLP) from 1 June 1987 to 20 January 1991; and from 20 January 1991 to 6 September 1994. The Barbados Labour Party (BLP) held office with the then Prime Minister, Tom Adams from 2 September 1976 to 18 June 1981; and from 18 June 1981 until his sudden death in office on 11 March 1985. The 3rd Prime Minister, Sir. Harold St. John took over with the Barbados Labour Party government (BLP) from 11 March 1985 to 28 May 1986. The BLP held power from 6 September 1994 to 15 January 2008. The Democratic Labour Party government (DLP) held power with the then 6th Prime Minister, David Thompson from 15 January 2008 until his death in office on 23 October 2010. The 7th Prime Minister, Freundel Stuart took over with the Democratic Labour Party government (DLP) from 23 October 2010 to 21 February 2013; and from 21 February 2013 to 24 May 2018 for the general elections for the new Barbados Labour Party (BLP). All of Barbados' Prime Ministers, except Freundel Stuart, held under the Ministry of Finance's portfolio. The Barbados Labour Party government (BLP) held power with the now 8th Prime Minister of Barbados, Mia Mottley from 24 May 2018 to present until the next general election on 24 May 2023. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Barbados" title="Foreign relations of Barbados">Foreign relations of Barbados</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Barbados follows a policy of <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">nonalignment</a> and seeks cooperative relations with all friendly states. Barbados is a full and participating member of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">Caribbean Community</a> (CARICOM), <a href="/wiki/CARICOM_Single_Market_and_Economy" title="CARICOM Single Market and Economy">CARICOM Single Market and Economy</a> (CSME), and the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Caribbean_States" title="Association of Caribbean States">Association of Caribbean States</a> (ACS).<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a> (OAS), <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Court_of_Justice" title="Caribbean Court of Justice">Caribbean Court of Justice</a> (CCJ). In 2005 the Parliament of Barbados voted on a measure replacing the UK's <a href="/wiki/Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council" title="Judicial Committee of the Privy Council">Judicial Committee of the Privy Council</a> with the Caribbean Court of Justice based in <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Spain" title="Port of Spain">Port of Spain</a>, Trinidad and Tobago. </p> 
      <h4><span id="World_Trade_Organization.2C_European_Commission.2C_CARIFORUM"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Trade_Organization,_European_Commission,_CARIFORUM">World Trade Organization, European Commission, CARIFORUM</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: World Trade Organization, European Commission, CARIFORUM">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Barbados is an original member (1995) of the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (WTO) and participates actively in its work. It grants at least MFN treatment to all its trading partners. <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> relations and cooperation with Barbados are carried out both on a bilateral and a regional basis. Barbados is party to the <a href="/wiki/Cotonou_Agreement" title="Cotonou Agreement">Cotonou Agreement</a>, through which As of December&nbsp;2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> it is linked by an <a href="/wiki/Economic_Partnership_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic Partnership Agreement">Economic Partnership Agreement</a> with the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>. The pact involves the Caribbean Forum (CARIFORUM) subgroup of the <a href="/wiki/African,_Caribbean_and_Pacific_Group_of_States" class="mw-redirect" title="African, Caribbean and Pacific Group of States">African, Caribbean and Pacific Group of States</a> (ACP). CARIFORUM is the only part of the wider ACP-bloc that has concluded the full regional trade-pact with the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. There are also ongoing EU-<a href="/wiki/Community_of_Latin_American_and_Caribbean_States" title="Community of Latin American and Caribbean States">Community of Latin American and Caribbean States</a> (CELAC) and EU-<a href="/wiki/CARIFORUM" title="CARIFORUM">CARIFORUM</a> dialogues.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Trade policy has also sought to protect a small number of domestic activities, mostly food production, from foreign competition, while recognising that most domestic needs are best met by imports. </p> 
      <h4><span id="The_Double_Taxation_Relief_.28CARICOM.29_Treaty_1994"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Double_Taxation_Relief_(CARICOM)_Treaty_1994">The Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty 1994</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: The Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty 1994">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>On 6 July 1994, at the Sherbourne Conference Centre, St. Michael, Barbados, representatives of eight (8) countries signed the Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaties 1994. The countries which were represented were: Antigua and Barbuda, Belize, Grenada, Jamaica, St. Kitts and Nevis, St. Lucia, St. Vincent and the Grenadines and Trinidad and Tobago.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 19 August 1994 a representative of the Government of Guyana signed a similar treaty. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Barbados_Defence_Force" title="Barbados Defence Force">Barbados Defence Force</a> has roughly 800 members. Within it, 14- to 18-year-olds make up the Barbados Cadet Corps. The defence preparations of the island nation are closely tied to defence treaties with the United Kingdom, the United States, and the People's Republic of China.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Barbados_Police_Force" title="Royal Barbados Police Force">Royal Barbados Police Force</a> is the sole law enforcement agency on the island of Barbados. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Barbados" title="Parishes of Barbados">Parishes of Barbados</a>
      </div>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Barbados" title="Economy of Barbados">Economy of Barbados</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sandy_Lane.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Sandy_Lane.jpg/260px-Sandy_Lane.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Sandy_Lane.jpg/390px-Sandy_Lane.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Sandy_Lane.jpg/520px-Sandy_Lane.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sandy_Lane.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Sandy_Lane_(resort)" title="Sandy Lane (resort)">Sandy Lane</a> is a leading resort in Barbados's tourism sector.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Barbados.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Tree_map_export_2009_Barbados.jpeg/300px-Tree_map_export_2009_Barbados.jpeg" decoding="async" width="300" height="234" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Tree_map_export_2009_Barbados.jpeg/450px-Tree_map_export_2009_Barbados.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Tree_map_export_2009_Barbados.jpeg/600px-Tree_map_export_2009_Barbados.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1106" data-file-height="864"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Barbados.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A proportional representation of national exports
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Barbados is the 53rd <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita">richest country in the world</a> in terms of GDP (Gross Domestic Product) per capita,<sup id="cite_ref-imf2_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf2-100">[100]</a></sup> has a well-developed <a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixed economy</a>, and a moderately high <a href="/wiki/Standard_of_living" title="Standard of living">standard of living</a>. According to the World Bank, Barbados is classified as being in its 66 top <a href="/wiki/High_income_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="High income economy">high income economies</a> of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (August 2018)">failed verification</span></a></i>]</sup> Despite this, a 2012 self-study in conjunction with the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Development_Bank" title="Caribbean Development Bank">Caribbean Development Bank</a> revealed 20% of Barbadians live in poverty, and nearly 10% cannot meet their basic daily food needs.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Historically, the economy of Barbados had been dependent on <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a> cultivation and related activities, but since the late 1970s and early 1980s it has diversified into the manufacturing and tourism sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> Offshore finance and information services have become important foreign exchange earners, and there is a healthy light manufacturing sector. Since the 1990s the Barbados Government has been seen as business-friendly and economically sound.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The island saw a construction boom, with the development and redevelopment of hotels, office complexes, and homes, partly due to the staging of the 2007 Cricket World Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> This slowed during the 2008 to 2012 world economic crisis and the recession.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There was a strong economy between 1999 and 2000 but the economy went into recession in 2001 and 2002 due to slowdowns in tourism, consumer spending and the impact of the <a href="/wiki/11_September_2001_attacks" class="mw-redirect" title="11 September 2001 attacks">11 September 2001 attacks</a> in the United States and the <a href="/wiki/7_July_2005_London_bombings" title="7 July 2005 London bombings">7 July 2005 London bombings</a> in the United Kingdom. The economy rebounded in 2003 and has shown growth since 2004 which continued right through to 2008. The economy went into recession again from 2008 to 2013 before showing growth from 2014 to 2017. Then it declined to another recession from 2017 to 2019 during the world economic crisis. There were 23 downgrades by both Standard &amp; Poor's and Moody's in 2016, 2017 and 2018. The economy showed signs of recovery with 3 upgrades from Standard and Poor's and Moody's in 2019. From 1 January to 31 March 2020 the economy had started to grow, but then it experienced another decline due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_recession" title="COVID-19 recession">COVID-19 economic recession</a>. </p>
      <p>Traditional trading partners include Canada, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">Caribbean Community</a> (especially <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>), the United Kingdom and the United States. Recent government administrations have continued efforts to reduce unemployment, encourage <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a>, and privatise remaining state-owned enterprises. Unemployment was reduced to 10.7% in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-1">[1]</a></sup> However, it has since increased to 11.9% in second quarter, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The European Union is assisting Barbados with a €10 million program of modernisation of the country's International Business and Financial Services Sector.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Barbados maintains the third largest <a href="/wiki/Barbados_Stock_Exchange" title="Barbados Stock Exchange">stock exchange</a> in the Caribbean region. As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, officials at the stock exchange were investigating the possibility of augmenting the local exchange with an International Securities Market (ISM) venture.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sovereign_default_and_restructuring">Sovereign default and restructuring</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Sovereign default and restructuring">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>By May 2018, Barbados' outstanding debt climbed to <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$7.5 billion</span>, more than 1.7 times the country's <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a>. In June 2018 the government defaulted on its sovereign debt when it failed to make a coupon on <a href="/wiki/Eurobond_(international)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurobond (international)">Eurobonds</a> maturing in 2035. Outstanding bond debt of Barbados reached <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$4.4 billion</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In October 2019, Barbados concluded restructuring negotiations with a creditor group including investments funds <a href="/wiki/Eaton_Vance" title="Eaton Vance">Eaton Vance Management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greylock_Capital_Management" title="Greylock Capital Management">Greylock Capital Management</a>, Teachers Advisors and Guyana Bank for Trade and Industry. Creditors will exchange existing bonds for a new debt series maturing in 2029. The new bonds involve a principal "haircut" of approximately 26% and include a clause allowing for deferment of principal and capitalization of interest in the event of a natural disaster.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Barbados has many health centers. However, the main hospital on the island is The Queen Elizabeth Hospital. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Barbados" title="Education in Barbados">Education in Barbados</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Christ_Church,_Barbados_014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Christ_Church%2C_Barbados_014.jpg/220px-Christ_Church%2C_Barbados_014.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Christ_Church%2C_Barbados_014.jpg/330px-Christ_Church%2C_Barbados_014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Christ_Church%2C_Barbados_014.jpg/440px-Christ_Church%2C_Barbados_014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Christ_Church,_Barbados_014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Schoolchildren in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Philip,_Barbados" title="Saint Philip, Barbados">Saint Philip, Barbados</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Barbados <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_literacy_rate" title="List of countries by literacy rate">literacy rate</a> is ranked close to 100%.<sup id="cite_ref-unesco_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unesco-112">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> The mainstream public education system of Barbados is fashioned after the British model. The government of Barbados spends 6.7% of its GDP on education (2008).<sup id="cite_ref-cia_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>All young people in the country must attend school until age 16. Barbados has over 70 primary schools and over 20 secondary schools throughout the island. There is a number of private schools, including <a href="/wiki/Montessori_education" title="Montessori education">Montessori</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Baccalaureate" title="International Baccalaureate">International Baccalaureate</a>. Student enrolment at these schools represents less than 5% of the total enrolment of the public schools. </p>
      <p>Certificate-, diploma- and degree-level education in the country is provided by the <a href="/wiki/Barbados_Community_College" title="Barbados Community College">Barbados Community College</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Jackman_Prescod_Institute_of_Technology" title="Samuel Jackman Prescod Institute of Technology">Samuel Jackman Prescod Institute of Technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Codrington_College" title="Codrington College">Codrington College</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_West_Indies,_Cave_Hill_Campus" class="mw-redirect" title="University of the West Indies, Cave Hill Campus">Cave Hill campus</a> and Open Campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_West_Indies" title="University of the West Indies">University of the West Indies</a>. Barbados is also home to several overseas medical schools, such as <a href="/wiki/Ross_University_School_of_Medicine" title="Ross University School of Medicine">Ross University School of Medicine</a> and the <a href="/wiki/American_University_of_Integrative_Sciences" title="American University of Integrative Sciences">American University of Integrative Sciences, School of Medicine</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Educational_testing">Educational testing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Educational testing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Barbados Secondary School Entrance Examination: Children who are 11 years old but under 12 years old on 1 September in the year of the examination are required to write the examination as a means of allocation to secondary school. </p>
      <p>Caribbean Secondary Education Certificate (CSEC) examinations are usually taken by students after five years of secondary school and mark the end of standard secondary education. The CSEC examinations are equivalent to the Ordinary Level (O-Levels) examinations and are targeted toward students 16 and older. </p>
      <p>Caribbean Advanced Proficiency Examinations (CAPE) are taken by students who have completed their secondary education and wish to continue their studies. Students who sit for the CAPE usually possess CSEC or an equivalent certification. The CAPE is equivalent to the British Advanced Levels (A-Levels), voluntary qualifications that are intended for university entrance.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Barbados" title="Culture of Barbados">Culture of Barbados</a>
      </div> 
      <p><b>Barbados</b> is a blend of West African, Portuguese, Creole, Indian and British cultures. Citizens are officially called Barbadians. The term "Bajan" (pronounced BAY-jun) may have come from a localised pronunciation of the word Barbadian, which at times can sound more like "Bar-bajan"; or, more likely, from English <i><a href="/wiki/Bay" title="Bay">bay</a></i> ("bayling"), Portuguese <i lang="pt" title="Portuguese-language text"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/baiano" class="extiw" title="wikt:baiano">baiano</a></i>. </p>
      <p>The largest <a href="/wiki/Carnival" title="Carnival">carnival</a>-like cultural event that takes place on the island is the <a href="/wiki/Crop_Over" title="Crop Over">Crop Over</a> festival, which was established in 1974. As in many other Caribbean and Latin American countries, Crop Over is an important event for many people on the island, as well as the thousands of tourists that flock to there to participate in the annual events.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados_22-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica-_Barbados-22">[22]</a></sup> The festival includes musical competitions and other traditional activities, and features the majority of the island's homegrown <a href="/wiki/Calypso_music" title="Calypso music">calypso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soca_music" title="Soca music">soca music</a> for the year. The male and female Barbadians who harvested the most sugarcane are crowned as the King and Queen of the crop.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Crop Over gets under way at the beginning of July and ends with the costumed parade on Kadooment Day, held on the first Monday of August. New calypso/soca music is usually released and played more frequently from the beginning of May to coincide with the start of the festival.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Barbadian_cuisine" title="Barbadian cuisine">Barbadian cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mount_Gay_Rum_Visitors_Centre,_Spring_Garden_HWY,_Barbados-002.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Mount_Gay_Rum_Visitors_Centre%2C_Spring_Garden_HWY%2C_Barbados-002.jpg/220px-Mount_Gay_Rum_Visitors_Centre%2C_Spring_Garden_HWY%2C_Barbados-002.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Mount_Gay_Rum_Visitors_Centre%2C_Spring_Garden_HWY%2C_Barbados-002.jpg/330px-Mount_Gay_Rum_Visitors_Centre%2C_Spring_Garden_HWY%2C_Barbados-002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Mount_Gay_Rum_Visitors_Centre%2C_Spring_Garden_HWY%2C_Barbados-002.jpg/440px-Mount_Gay_Rum_Visitors_Centre%2C_Spring_Garden_HWY%2C_Barbados-002.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mount_Gay_Rum_Visitors_Centre,_Spring_Garden_HWY,_Barbados-002.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mount_Gay_Rum" title="Mount Gay Rum">Mount Gay Rum</a> visitors centre
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bajan cuisine is a mixture of <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuisine of Africa">African</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_cuisine" title="Indian cuisine">Indian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Irish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Creole_peoples" title="Creole peoples">Creole</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_cuisine" title="British cuisine">British</a> influences. A typical meal consists of a main dish of meat or fish, normally marinated with a mixture of herbs and spices, hot side dishes, and one or more salads. A common Bajan side dish could be pickled cucumber, fish cakes, bake, etc. The meal is usually served with one or more sauces.<sup id="cite_ref-Totally_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Totally-115">[115]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_dish" title="National dish">national dish</a> of Barbados is <a href="/wiki/Cou-cou" title="Cou-cou">cou-cou</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Flying_fish" title="Flying fish">flying fish</a> with spicy gravy.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Another traditional meal is "Pudding and Souse" a dish of pickled <a href="/wiki/Pork" title="Pork">pork</a> with spiced sweet potatoes.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> A wide variety of seafood and meats are also available. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Mount_Gay_Rum" title="Mount Gay Rum">Mount Gay Rum</a> visitors centre in Barbados claims to be the world's oldest remaining rum company, with earliest confirmed deed from 1703. <a href="/wiki/Cockspur_Rum" title="Cockspur Rum">Cockspur Rum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malibu_(rum)" title="Malibu (rum)">Malibu</a> are also from the island. Barbados is home to the <a href="/wiki/Banks_Barbados_Brewery" title="Banks Barbados Brewery">Banks Barbados Brewery</a>, which brews Banks Beer, a <a href="/wiki/Pale_lager" title="Pale lager">pale lager</a>, as well as Banks <a href="/wiki/Amber_Ale" class="mw-redirect" title="Amber Ale">Amber Ale</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> Banks also brews Tiger Malt, a non-alcoholic <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">malted beverage</a>. 10 Saints beer is brewed in <a href="/wiki/Speightstown" title="Speightstown">Speightstown</a>, St. Peter in Barbados and aged for 90 days in Mount Gay 'Special Reserve' Rum casks. It was first brewed in 2009 and is available in certain Caricom nations.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Barbados" title="Music of Barbados">Music of Barbados</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rihanna-brisbane.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Rihanna-brisbane.jpg/220px-Rihanna-brisbane.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Rihanna-brisbane.jpg/330px-Rihanna-brisbane.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Rihanna-brisbane.jpg/440px-Rihanna-brisbane.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rihanna-brisbane.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>International <a href="/wiki/Celebrity" title="Celebrity">pop star</a> <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>, a native of Barbados is a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy awards">nine-time Grammy Award winner</a> and one of the <a href="/wiki/Best_selling_music_artists" class="mw-redirect" title="Best selling music artists">best selling music artists</a> of all time, selling over 200&nbsp;million records worldwide. In 2009 she was appointed as an Honorary Ambassador of Youth and Culture for Barbados by the late Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/David_Thompson_(Barbadian_politician)" title="David Thompson (Barbadian politician)">David Thompson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="excerpt-block">
       <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r952607947">.mw-parser-output .excerpt .selflink{font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .excerpt-indicator{border-left:3px solid #c8ccd1;margin:1em 0;padding-left:1em}</style>
       <div class="excerpt"> 
        <p>The <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Barbados" title="Music of Barbados">music of Barbados</a> includes distinctive national styles of <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Popular_music" title="Popular music">popular music</a>, including elements of <a href="/wiki/Western_classical_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Western classical music">Western classical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Religious_music" title="Religious music">religious music</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Barbados" title="Culture of Barbados">culture of Barbados</a> is a syncretic mix of African and British elements, and the island's music reflects this mix through song types and styles, instrumentation, dances, and aesthetic principles.. </p> Barbadian folk traditions include the <a href="/wiki/Landship_(Barbados)" class="mw-redirect" title="Landship (Barbados)">Landship</a> movement, which is a satirical, informal organization based on the <a href="/wiki/British_navy" class="mw-redirect" title="British navy">British navy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tea_meeting" title="Tea meeting">tea meetings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tuk_band" title="Tuk band">tuk</a> bands and numerous traditional songs and dances. In modern Barbados, popular styles include <a href="/wiki/Calypso_music" title="Calypso music">calypso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spouge" title="Spouge">spouge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_folk" class="mw-redirect" title="Contemporary folk">contemporary folk</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_music" title="World music">world music</a>. Barbados is, along with Guadeloupe, Martinique, Trinidad, Cuba, Puerto Rico, and the Virgin Islands, one of the few centers for Caribbean jazz.
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_holidays">Public holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Public holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Barbados" title="Sport in Barbados">Sport in Barbados</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kensington_Oval_yes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Kensington_Oval_yes.jpg/220px-Kensington_Oval_yes.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Kensington_Oval_yes.jpg/330px-Kensington_Oval_yes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Kensington_Oval_yes.jpg/440px-Kensington_Oval_yes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kensington_Oval_yes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Kensington_Oval" title="Kensington Oval">Kensington Oval</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bridgetown" title="Bridgetown">Bridgetown</a> hosted the 2007 Cricket World Cup final. Cricket is one of the most followed games in Barbados and Kensington Oval is often referred to as the "Mecca in Cricket" due to its significance and contributions to the sport.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Horesandjockey.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Horesandjockey.jpg/220px-Horesandjockey.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Horesandjockey.jpg/330px-Horesandjockey.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Horesandjockey.jpg/440px-Horesandjockey.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2218" data-file-height="1584"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Horesandjockey.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A horse and rider at Garrison Savannah
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As in other Caribbean countries of British colonial heritage, <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> is very popular on the island. The <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_cricket_team" title="West Indies cricket team">West Indies cricket team</a> usually includes several Barbadian players. In addition to several warm-up matches and six "Super Eight" matches, the country hosted the final of the 2007 Cricket World Cup. Barbados has produced many great cricketers including <a href="/wiki/Sir_Garfield_Sobers" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Garfield Sobers">Sir Garfield Sobers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sir_Frank_Worrell" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Frank Worrell">Sir Frank Worrell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sir_Clyde_Walcott" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Clyde Walcott">Sir Clyde Walcott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sir_Everton_Weekes" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Everton Weekes">Sir Everton Weekes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Greenidge" title="Gordon Greenidge">Gordon Greenidge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wes_Hall" title="Wes Hall">Wes Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Griffith" title="Charlie Griffith">Charlie Griffith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joel_Garner" title="Joel Garner">Joel Garner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Desmond_Haynes" title="Desmond Haynes">Desmond Haynes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Marshall" title="Malcolm Marshall">Malcolm Marshall</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">Rugby</a> is also popular in Barbados. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Horse_racing" title="Horse racing">Horse racing</a> takes place at the <a href="/wiki/Garrison_Savannah_Racetrack" title="Garrison Savannah Racetrack">Historic Garrison Savannah</a> close to Bridgetown. Spectators can pay for admission to the stands, or else can watch races from the public "rail", which encompasses the track. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">Basketball</a> is an increasingly popular sport, played at school or college. <a href="/wiki/Barbados_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbados national basketball team">Barbados's national team</a> has shown some unexpected results as in the past it beat many much larger countries. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Polo" title="Polo">Polo</a> is very popular amongst the rich elite on the island and the "High-Goal" Apes Hill team is based at the St James's Club.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> It is also played at the private <a href="/wiki/Holders_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Holders Festival">Holders Festival</a> ground. </p>
      <p>In golf, the <a href="/wiki/Barbados_Open" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbados Open">Barbados Open</a>, played at Royal Westmoreland Golf Club, was an annual stop on the <a href="/wiki/European_Seniors_Tour" class="mw-redirect" title="European Seniors Tour">European Seniors Tour</a> from 2000 to 2009. In December 2006 the <a href="/wiki/WGC-World_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="WGC-World Cup">WGC-World Cup</a> took place at the country's <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Lane_(resort)" title="Sandy Lane (resort)">Sandy Lane</a> resort on the Country Club course, an 18-hole course designed by <a href="/wiki/Tom_Fazio" title="Tom Fazio">Tom Fazio</a>. The Barbados Golf Club is another course on the island. It has hosted the Barbados Open on several occasions. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">Volleyball</a> is also popular and is mainly played indoors. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">Tennis</a> is gaining popularity and Barbados is home to <a href="/wiki/Darian_King" title="Darian King">Darian King</a>, currently ranked 270th in the world and is the 2nd highest ranked player in the Caribbean. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Motorsports" class="mw-redirect" title="Motorsports">Motorsports</a> also play a role, with Rally Barbados occurring each summer and being listed on the FIA NACAM calendar. Also, the <a href="/wiki/Bushy_Park,_Barbados" class="mw-redirect" title="Bushy Park, Barbados">Bushy Park Circuit</a> hosted the <a href="/wiki/Race_of_Champions" title="Race of Champions">Race of Champions</a> and <a href="/wiki/Global_RallyCross_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Global RallyCross Championship">Global RallyCross Championship</a> in 2014. </p>
      <p>The presence of the trade winds along with favourable swells make the southern tip of the island an ideal location for wave sailing (an extreme form of the sport of <a href="/wiki/Windsurfing" title="Windsurfing">windsurfing</a>). </p>
      <p>Barbados also hosts several international <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.visitbarbados.org/world-surfing-league-barbados-surf-pro">surfing competitions</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">Netball</a> is also popular with women in Barbados. </p>
      <p>Barbadian team The Flyin' Fish, are the 2009 <a href="/wiki/Segway_polo" title="Segway polo">Segway polo</a> World Champions.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">November 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Barbados" title="Transport in Barbados">Transport in Barbados</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Barbados_Midibus1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Barbados_Midibus1.jpg/220px-Barbados_Midibus1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Barbados_Midibus1.jpg/330px-Barbados_Midibus1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Barbados_Midibus1.jpg/440px-Barbados_Midibus1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2764" data-file-height="2160"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Barbados_Midibus1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Hino ACME Minibus B 163 in Speightstown, St. Peter, Barbados
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Although Barbados is about 34&nbsp;km (21&nbsp;mi) across at its widest point, a car journey from Six Cross Roads in St. Philip (south-east) to North Point in St. Lucy (north-central) can take one and a half hours or longer due to traffic. Barbados has half as many registered cars as citizens. In Barbados, drivers drive on the left side of the road. </p>
      <p>Barbados is known for its many roundabouts. One famous roundabout is a roundabout located east of Bridgetown, where you will see an emancipation statue of a slave named Bussa. </p>
      <p>Transport on the island is relatively convenient with "<a href="/wiki/Share_taxis" class="mw-redirect" title="Share taxis">route taxis</a>" called "ZRs" (pronounced "Zed-Rs") travelling to most points on the island. These small buses can at times be crowded, as passengers are generally never turned down regardless of the number. They will usually take the more scenic routes to destinations. They generally depart from the capital <a href="/wiki/Bridgetown" title="Bridgetown">Bridgetown</a> or from <a href="/wiki/Speightstown,_Barbados" class="mw-redirect" title="Speightstown, Barbados">Speightstown</a> in the northern part of the island. </p>
      <p>Including the ZRs, there are three bus systems running seven days a week (though less frequently on Sundays). There are ZRs, the yellow minibuses and the blue <a href="/wiki/Barbados_Transport_Board" title="Barbados Transport Board">Transport Board buses</a>. A ride on any of them costs Bds$&nbsp;3.5.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> The smaller buses from the two privately owned systems ("ZRs" and "minibuses") can give change; the larger blue buses from the government-operated <a href="/wiki/Barbados_Transport_Board" title="Barbados Transport Board">Barbados Transport Board</a> system cannot, but do give receipts. The Barbados Transport Board buses travel in regular bus routes and scheduled timetables across Barbados. Schoolchildren in school uniform including some Secondary schools ride for free on the government buses and for Bds$&nbsp;2.5 on the ZRs. Most routes require a connection in Bridgetown. Barbados Transport Board's headquarters are located at Kay's House, Roebuck Street, St. Michael, and the bus depots and terminals are located in the Fairchild Street Bus Terminal in Fairchild Street and the Princess Alice Bus Terminal (which was formerly the Lower Green Bus Terminal in Jubilee Gardens, Bridgetown, St. Michael) in Princess Alice Highway, Bridgetown, St. Michael; the Speightstown Bus Terminal in Speightstown, St. Peter; the Oistins Bus Depot in Oistins, Christ Church; and the Mangrove Bus Depot in Mangrove, St. Philip. In July 2020, the <a href="/wiki/Barbados_Transport_Board" title="Barbados Transport Board">Barbados Transport Board</a> received 33 <a href="/wiki/BYD_Auto" title="BYD Auto">BYD</a> electric buses which were obtained not only to add to the aging fleet of diesel buses but also to assist the Government in their goal of eliminating the use of fossil fuels by the year 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Some hotels also provide visitors with shuttles to points of interest on the island from outside the hotel lobby. There are several locally owned and operated vehicle rental agencies in Barbados but there are no multi-national companies. </p>
      <p>The island's lone airport is the <a href="/wiki/Grantley_Adams_International_Airport" title="Grantley Adams International Airport">Grantley Adams International Airport</a>. It receives daily flights by several major airlines from points around the globe, as well as several smaller regional commercial airlines and charters. The airport serves as the main air-transportation hub for the eastern Caribbean. In the first decade of the 21st century it underwent a <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$100 million</span> upgrade and expansion in February 2003 until completion in August 2005. </p>
      <p>There was also a helicopter shuttle service, which offered air taxi services to a number of sites around the island, mainly on the West Coast tourist belt. Air and maritime traffic was regulated by the <a href="/wiki/Barbados_Port_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbados Port Authority">Barbados Port Authority</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Barbados&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Barbadian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbadian people">Barbadian people</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Barbados" class="mw-redirect" title="List of people from Barbados">List of people from Barbados</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Barbadian_Americans" title="List of Barbadian Americans">List of Barbadian Americans</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Barbadian_Britons" title="List of Barbadian Britons">List of Barbadian Britons</a>
      </div>

         <li id="cite_note-56"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-56">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFLogan" class="citation news cs1">Logan, Gabi. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://traveltips.usatoday.com/geologic-history-barbados-beaches-57660.html">"Geologic History of Barbados Beaches"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20120322063852/http://traveltips.usatoday.com/geologic-history-barbados-beaches-57660.html">Archived</a> from the original on 22 March 2012<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2 July</span> 2011</span>. <q>Barbados lies directly over the intersection of the Caribbean plate and the South American plate in a region known as a subduction zone. Beneath the ocean floor, the South American plate slowly slides below the Caribbean plate.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=USA+Today&amp;rft.atitle=Geologic+History+of+Barbados+Beaches&amp;rft.aulast=Logan&amp;rft.aufirst=Gabi&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Ftraveltips.usatoday.com%2Fgeologic-history-barbados-beaches-57660.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABarbados" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-57"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-57">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.barbadosbeachhouse.com/barbados_sightseeing_animal_flower_cave.php">"Barbados Sightseeing – Animal Flower Cave"</a>. <i>Leigh Designs</i>. Little Bay House. 2010. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20111212233710/http://www.barbadosbeachhouse.com/barbados_sightseeing_animal_flower_cave.php">Archived</a> from the original on 12 December 2011<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">10 July</span> 2011</span>. <q>The Animal flower Cave is the island's lone accessible sea-cave and was discovered from the sea in 1780 by two English explorers. The cave's coral floor is estimated to be 400,000 to 500,000 years old and the "younger" coral section above the floor is about 126,000 years old. The dating was carried out by the German Geographical Institute, and visitors can see a "map" of the dating work in the bar and restaurant. The cave now stands some six feet above the high tide mark even though it was formed at sea level. This is because Barbados is rising about one inch per 1,000 years, which is yet another indication of the cave's age.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Leigh+Designs&amp;rft.atitle=Barbados+Sightseeing+%E2%80%93+Animal+Flower+Cave&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.barbadosbeachhouse.com%2Fbarbados_sightseeing_animal_flower_cave.php&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABarbados" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li>

               <tr>
                <td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2">
                 <div>
                  <b>N.B.:</b> Territories in <i>italics</i> are parts of transregional sovereign states or non-sovereign dependencies. 
                  <p><sup>^</sup> These three <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Caribbean" title="Dutch Caribbean">Dutch Caribbean</a> territories form the <a href="/wiki/SSS_islands" title="SSS islands">SSS islands</a>. </p>
                  <p><sup>*</sup> These three <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Caribbean" title="Dutch Caribbean">Dutch Caribbean</a> territories form the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Netherlands" title="Caribbean Netherlands">BES islands</a>. </p>
                  <p><sup>†</sup> <a href="/wiki/Physical_geography" title="Physical geography">Physiographically</a>, these are <a href="/wiki/Island#Continental_islands" title="Island">continental islands</a> not a part of the volcanic Windward Islands arc. However, based on proximity, these islands are sometimes grouped with the <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a> culturally and politically. </p>
                  <p><sup>~</sup> <a href="/wiki/Territorial_dispute" title="Territorial dispute">Disputed territories</a> administered by <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>. </p>
                  <p><sup>#</sup> Physiographically, <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a> is an isolated <a href="/wiki/Island#Oceanic_islands" title="Island">oceanic island</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">North Atlantic Ocean</a>, not a part of the Antilles, West Indies, Caribbean, North American continental mainland or South American continental mainland. Usually grouped with Northern American countries based on proximity; occasionally grouped with the Caribbean region culturally. </p> <sup>ǂ</sup> <a href="/wiki/Territorial_dispute" title="Territorial dispute">Disputed territories</a> administered by <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>.
                 </div></td>
               </tr>
